051033 So I sent to you at once, and you have been kind enough to come. Now therefore we are all here present in the sight of God, to hear all that you have been commanded by the Lord."
051034 And Peter opened his mouth and said: "Truly I perceive that God shows no partiality,
051035 but in every nation any one who fears him and does what is right is acceptable to him.
051036 You know the word which he sent to Israel, preaching good news of peace by Jesus Christ (he is Lord of all),
051037 the word which was proclaimed throughout all Judea, beginning from Galilee after the baptism which John preached:
051038 how God anointed Jesus of Nazareth with the Holy Spirit and with power; how he went about doing good and healing all that were oppressed by the devil, for God was with him.
051039 And we are witnesses to all that he did both in the country of the Jews and in Jerusalem. They put him to death by hanging him on a tree;
051040 but God raised him on the third day and made him manifest;
051041 not to all the people but to us who were chosen by God as witnesses, who ate and drank with him after he rose from the dead.
051042 And he commanded us to preach to the people, and to testify that he is the one ordained by God to be judge of the living and the dead.
051043 To him all the prophets bear witness that every one who believes in him receives forgiveness of sins through his name."
051044 While Peter was still saying this, the Holy Spirit fell on all who heard the word.
051045 And the believers from among the circumcised who came with Peter were amazed, because the gift of the Holy Spirit had been poured out even on the Gentiles.
051046 For they heard them speaking in tongues and extolling God. Then Peter declared,
051047 "Can any one forbid water for baptizing these people who have received the Holy Spirit just as we have?"
051048 And he commanded them to be baptized in the name of Jesus Christ. Then they asked him to remain for some days.
051101 Now the apostles and the brethren who were in Judea heard that the Gentiles also had received the word of God.
051102 So when Peter went up to Jerusalem, the circumcision party criticized him,
051103 saying, "Why did you go to uncircumcised men and eat with them?"
051104 But Peter began and explained to them in order:
051105 "I was in the city of Joppa praying; and in a trance I saw a vision, something descending, like a great sheet, let down from heaven by four corners; and it came down to me.
051106 Looking at it closely I observed animals and beasts of prey and reptiles and birds of the air.
051107 And I heard a voice saying to me, 'Rise, Peter; kill and eat.'
051108 But I said, 'No, Lord; for nothing common or unclean has ever entered my mouth.'
051109 But the voice answered a second time from heaven, 'What God has cleansed you must not call common.'
051110 This happened three times, and all was drawn up again into heaven.
051111 At that very moment three men arrived at the house in which we were, sent to me from Caesare'a.
051112 And the Spirit told me to go with them, making no distinction. These six brethren also accompanied me, and we entered the man's house.
051113 And he told us how he had seen the angel standing in his house and saying, 'Send to Joppa and bring Simon called Peter;
051114 he will declare to you a message by which you will be saved, you and all your household.'
051115 As I began to speak, the Holy Spirit fell on them just as on us at the beginning.
051116 And I remembered the word of the Lord, how he said, 'John baptized with water, but you shall be baptized with the Holy Spirit.'
051117 If then God gave the same gift to them as he gave to us when we believed in the Lord Jesus Christ, who was I that I could withstand God?"
051118 When they heard this they were silenced. And they glorified God, saying, "Then to the Gentiles also God has granted repentance unto life."
051119 Now those who were scattered because of the persecution that arose over Stephen traveled as far as Phoeni'cia and Cyprus and Antioch, speaking the word to none except Jews.
051120 But there were some of them, men of Cyprus and Cyre'ne, who on coming to Antioch spoke to the Greeks also, preaching the Lord Jesus.
051121 And the hand of the Lord was with them, and a great number that believed turned to the Lord.
051122 News of this came to the ears of the church in Jerusalem, and they sent Barnabas to Antioch.
051123 When he came and saw the grace of God, he was glad; and he exhorted them all to remain faithful to the Lord with steadfast purpose;
051124 for he was a good man, full of the Holy Spirit and of faith. And a large company was added to the Lord.
051125 So Barnabas went to Tarsus to look for Saul;
051126 and when he had found him, he brought him to Antioch. For a whole year they met with the church, and taught a large company of people; and in Antioch the disciples were for the first time called Christians.
051127 Now in these days prophets came down from Jerusalem to Antioch.
051128 And one of them named Ag'abus stood up and foretold by the Spirit that there would be a great famine over all the world; and this took place in the days of Claudius.
051129 And the disciples determined, every one according to his ability, to send relief to the brethren who lived in Judea;
051130 and they did so, sending it to the elders by the hand of Barnabas and Saul.
051201 About that time Herod the king laid violent hands upon some who belonged to the church.
051202 He killed James the brother of John with the sword;
051203 and when he saw that it pleased the Jews, he proceeded to arrest Peter also. This was during the days of Unleavened Bread.
051204 And when he had seized him, he put him in prison, and delivered him to four squads of soldiers to guard him, intending after the Passover to bring him out to the people.
051205 So Peter was kept in prison; but earnest prayer for him was made to God by the church.
051206 The very night when Herod was about to bring him out, Peter was sleeping between two soldiers, bound with two chains, and sentries before the door were guarding the prison;
051207 and behold, an angel of the Lord appeared, and a light shone in the cell; and he struck Peter on the side and woke him, saying, "Get up quickly." And the chains fell off his hands.
051208 And the angel said to him, "Dress yourself and put on your sandals." And he did so. And he said to him, "Wrap your mantle around you and follow me."
051209 And he went out and followed him; he did not know that what was done by the angel was real, but thought he was seeing a vision.
051210 When they had passed the first and the second guard, they came to the iron gate leading into the city. It opened to them of its own accord, and they went out and passed on through one street; and immediately the angel left him.
051211 And Peter came to himself, and said, "Now I am sure that the Lord has sent his angel and rescued me from the hand of Herod and from all that the Jewish people were expecting."
051212 When he realized this, he went to the house of Mary, the mother of John whose other name was Mark, where many were gathered together and were praying.
051213 And when he knocked at the door of the gateway, a maid named Rhoda came to answer.
051214 Recognizing Peter's voice, in her joy she did not open the gate but ran in and told that Peter was standing at the gate.
051215 They said to her, "You are mad." But she insisted that it was so. They said, "It is his angel!"
051216 But Peter continued knocking; and when they opened, they saw him and were amazed.
051217 But motioning to them with his hand to be silent, he described to them how the Lord had brought him out of the prison. And he said, "Tell this to James and to the brethren." Then he departed and went to another place.
051218 Now when day came, there was no small stir among the soldiers over what had become of Peter.
051219 And when Herod had sought for him and could not find him, he examined the sentries and ordered that they should be put to death. Then he went down from Judea to Caesare'a, and remained there.
051220 Now Herod was angry with the people of Tyre and Sidon; and they came to him in a body, and having persuaded Blastus, the king's chamberlain, they asked for peace, because their country depended on the king's country for food.
051221 On an appointed day Herod put on his royal robes, took his seat upon the throne, and made an oration to them.
051222 And the people shouted, "The voice of a god, and not of man!"
051223 Immediately an angel of the Lord smote him, because he did not give God the glory; and he was eaten by worms and died.
051224 But the word of God grew and multiplied.
051225 And Barnabas and Saul returned from Jerusalem when they had fulfilled their mission, bringing with them John whose other name was Mark.
051301 Now in the church at Antioch there were prophets and teachers, Barnabas, Simeon who was called Niger, Lucius of Cyre'ne, Man'a-en a member of the court of Herod the tetrarch, and Saul.
051302 While they were worshiping the Lord and fasting, the Holy Spirit said, "Set apart for me Barnabas and Saul for the work to which I have called them."
051303 Then after fasting and praying they laid their hands on them and sent them off.
051304 So, being sent out by the Holy Spirit, they went down to Seleu'cia; and from there they sailed to Cyprus.
051305 When they arrived at Sal'amis, they proclaimed the word of God in the synagogues of the Jews. And they had John to assist them.
051306 When they had gone through the whole island as far as Paphos, they came upon a certain magician, a Jewish false prophet, named Bar-Jesus.
051307 He was with the proconsul, Sergius Paulus, a man of intelligence, who summoned Barnabas and Saul and sought to hear the word of God.
051308 But El'ymas the magician (for that is the meaning of his name) withstood them, seeking to turn away the proconsul from the faith.
051309 But Saul, who is also called Paul, filled with the Holy Spirit, looked intently at him
051310 and said, "You son of the devil, you enemy of all righteousness, full of all deceit and villainy, will you not stop making crooked the straight paths of the Lord?
051311 And now, behold, the hand of the Lord is upon you, and you shall be blind and unable to see the sun for a time." Immediately mist and darkness fell upon him and he went about seeking people to lead him by the hand.
051312 Then the proconsul believed, when he saw what had occurred, for he was astonished at the teaching of the Lord.
051313 Now Paul and his company set sail from Paphos, and came to Perga in Pamphyl'ia. And John left them and returned to Jerusalem;
051314 but they passed on from Perga and came to Antioch of Pisid'ia. And on the sabbath day they went into the synagogue and sat down.
051315 After the reading of the law and the prophets, the rulers of the synagogue sent to them, saying, "Brethren, if you have any word of exhortation for the people, say it."
051316 So Paul stood up, and motioning with his hand said: "Men of Israel, and you that fear God, listen.
051317 The God of this people Israel chose our fathers and made the people great during their stay in the land of Egypt, and with uplifted arm he led them out of it.
051318 And for about forty years he bore with them in the wilderness.
051319 And when he had destroyed seven nations in the land of Canaan, he gave them their land as an inheritance, for about four hundred and fifty years.
051320 And after that he gave them judges until Samuel the prophet.
051321 Then they asked for a king; and God gave them Saul the son of Kish, a man of the tribe of Benjamin, for forty years.
051322 And when he had removed him, he raised up David to be their king; of whom he testified and said, 'I have found in David the son of Jesse a man after my heart, who will do all my will.'
051323 Of this man's posterity God has brought to Israel a Savior, Jesus, as he promised.
051324 Before his coming John had preached a baptism of repentance to all the people of Israel.
051325 And as John was finishing his course, he said, 'What do you suppose that I am? I am not he. No, but after me one is coming, the sandals of whose feet I am not worthy to untie.'
051326 "Brethren, sons of the family of Abraham, and those among you that fear God, to us has been sent the message of this salvation.
051327 For those who live in Jerusalem and their rulers, because they did not recognize him nor understand the utterances of the prophets which are read every sabbath, fulfilled these by condemning him.
051328 Though they could charge him with nothing deserving death, yet they asked Pilate to have him killed.
051329 And when they had fulfilled all that was written of him, they took him down from the tree, and laid him in a tomb.
051330 But God raised him from the dead;
051331 and for many days he appeared to those who came up with him from Galilee to Jerusalem, who are now his witnesses to the people.
051332 And we bring you the good news that what God promised to the fathers,
051333 this he has fulfilled to us their children by raising Jesus; as also it is written in the second psalm, 'Thou art my Son, today I have begotten thee.'
051334 And as for the fact that he raised him from the dead, no more to return to corruption, he spoke in this way, 'I will give you the holy and sure blessings of David.'
051335 Therefore he says also in another psalm, 'Thou wilt not let thy Holy One see corruption.'
051336 For David, after he had served the counsel of God in his own generation, fell asleep, and was laid with his fathers, and saw corruption;
051337 but he whom God raised up saw no corruption.
051338 Let it be known to you therefore, brethren, that through this man forgiveness of sins is proclaimed to you,
051339 and by him every one that believes is freed from everything from which you could not be freed by the law of Moses.
051340 Beware, therefore, lest there come upon you what is said in the prophets:
051341 'Behold, you scoffers, and wonder, and perish; for I do a deed in your days, a deed you will never believe, if one declares it to you.'"
051342 As they went out, the people begged that these things might be told them the next sabbath.
051343 And when the meeting of the synagogue broke up, many Jews and devout converts to Judaism followed Paul and Barnabas, who spoke to them and urged them to continue in the grace of God.
051344 The next sabbath almost the whole city gathered together to hear the word of God.
051345 But when the Jews saw the multitudes, they were filled with jealousy, and contradicted what was spoken by Paul, and reviled him.
051346 And Paul and Barnabas spoke out boldly, saying, "It was necessary that the word of God should be spoken first to you. Since you thrust it from you, and judge yourselves unworthy of eternal life, behold, we turn to the Gentiles.
051347 For so the Lord has commanded us, saying, 'I have set you to be a light for the Gentiles, that you may bring salvation to the uttermost parts of the earth.'"
051348 And when the Gentiles heard this, they were glad and glorified the word of God; and as many as were ordained to eternal life believed.
051349 And the word of the Lord spread throughout all the region.
051350 But the Jews incited the devout women of high standing and the leading men of the city, and stirred up persecution against Paul and Barnabas, and drove them out of their district.
051351 But they shook off the dust from their feet against them, and went to Ico'nium.
051352 And the disciples were filled with joy and with the Holy Spirit.
051401 Now at Ico'nium they entered together into the Jewish synagogue, and so spoke that a great company believed, both of Jews and of Greeks.
051402 But the unbelieving Jews stirred up the Gentiles and poisoned their minds against the brethren.
051403 So they remained for a long time, speaking boldly for the Lord, who bore witness to the word of his grace, granting signs and wonders to be done by their hands.
051404 But the people of the city were divided; some sided with the Jews, and some with the apostles.
051405 When an attempt was made by both Gentiles and Jews, with their rulers, to molest them and to stone them,
051406 they learned of it and fled to Lystra and Derbe, cities of Lycao'nia, and to the surrounding country;
051407 and there they preached the gospel.
051408 Now at Lystra there was a man sitting, who could not use his feet; he was a cripple from birth, who had never walked.
051409 He listened to Paul speaking; and Paul, looking intently at him and seeing that he had faith to be made well,
051410 said in a loud voice, "Stand upright on your feet." And he sprang up and walked.
051411 And when the crowds saw what Paul had done, they lifted up their voices, saying in Lycao'nian, "The gods have come down to us in the likeness of men!"
051412 Barnabas they called Zeus, and Paul, because he was the chief speaker, they called Hermes.
051413 And the priest of Zeus, whose temple was in front of the city, brought oxen and garlands to the gates and wanted to offer sacrifice with the people.
051414 But when the apostles Barnabas and Paul heard of it, they tore their garments and rushed out among the multitude, crying,
051415 "Men, why are you doing this? We also are men, of like nature with you, and bring you good news, that you should turn from these vain things to a living God who made the heaven and the earth and the sea and all that is in them.
051416 In past generations he allowed all the nations to walk in their own ways;
051417 yet he did not leave himself without witness, for he did good and gave you from heaven rains and fruitful seasons, satisfying your hearts with food and gladness."
051418 With these words they scarcely restrained the people from offering sacrifice to them.
051419 But Jews came there from Antioch and Ico'nium; and having persuaded the people, they stoned Paul and dragged him out of the city, supposing that he was dead.
051420 But when the disciples gathered about him, he rose up and entered the city; and on the next day he went on with Barnabas to Derbe.
051421 When they had preached the gospel to that city and had made many disciples, they returned to Lystra and to Ico'nium and to Antioch,
051422 strengthening the souls of the disciples, exhorting them to continue in the faith, and saying that through many tribulations we must enter the kingdom of God.
051423 And when they had appointed elders for them in every church, with prayer and fasting they committed them to the Lord in whom they believed.
051424 Then they passed through Pisid'ia, and came to Pamphyl'ia.
051425 And when they had spoken the word in Perga, they went down to Attali'a;
051426 and from there they sailed to Antioch, where they had been commended to the grace of God for the work which they had fulfilled.
051427 And when they arrived, they gathered the church together and declared all that God had done with them, and how he had opened a door of faith to the Gentiles.
051428 And they remained no little time with the disciples.
051501 But some men came down from Judea and were teaching the brethren, "Unless you are circumcised according to the custom of Moses, you cannot be saved."
051502 And when Paul and Barnabas had no small dissension and debate with them, Paul and Barnabas and some of the others were appointed to go up to Jerusalem to the apostles and the elders about this question.
051503 So, being sent on their way by the church, they passed through both Phoeni'cia and Sama'ria, reporting the conversion of the Gentiles, and they gave great joy to all the brethren.
051504 When they came to Jerusalem, they were welcomed by the church and the apostles and the elders, and they declared all that God had done with them.
051505 But some believers who belonged to the party of the Pharisees rose up, and said, "It is necessary to circumcise them, and to charge them to keep the law of Moses."
051506 The apostles and the elders were gathered together to consider this matter.
051507 And after there had been much debate, Peter rose and said to them, "Brethren, you know that in the early days God made choice among you, that by my mouth the Gentiles should hear the word of the gospel and believe.
051508 And God who knows the heart bore witness to them, giving them the Holy Spirit just as he did to us;
051509 and he made no distinction between us and them, but cleansed their hearts by faith.
051510 Now therefore why do you make trial of God by putting a yoke upon the neck of the disciples which neither our fathers nor we have been able to bear?
051511 But we believe that we shall be saved through the grace of the Lord Jesus, just as they will."
051512 And all the assembly kept silence; and they listened to Barnabas and Paul as they related what signs and wonders God had done through them among the Gentiles.
051513 After they finished speaking, James replied, "Brethren, listen to me.
051514 Simeon has related how God first visited the Gentiles, to take out of them a people for his name.
051515 And with this the words of the prophets agree, as it is written,
051516 'After this I will return, and I will rebuild the dwelling of David, which has fallen; I will rebuild its ruins, and I will set it up,
051517 that the rest of men may seek the Lord, and all the Gentiles who are called by my name,
051518 says the Lord, who has made these things known from of old.'
051519 Therefore my judgment is that we should not trouble those of the Gentiles who turn to God,
051520 but should write to them to abstain from the pollutions of idols and from unchastity and from what is strangled and from blood.
051521 For from early generations Moses has had in every city those who preach him, for he is read every sabbath in the synagogues."
051522 Then it seemed good to the apostles and the elders, with the whole church, to choose men from among them and send them to Antioch with Paul and Barnabas. They sent Judas called Barsab'bas, and Silas, leading men among the brethren,
051523 with the following letter: "The brethren, both the apostles and the elders, to the brethren who are of the Gentiles in Antioch and Syria and Cili'cia, greeting.
051524 Since we have heard that some persons from us have troubled you with words, unsettling your minds, although we gave them no instructions,
051525 it has seemed good to us, having come to one accord, to choose men and send them to you with our beloved Barnabas and Paul,
051526 men who have risked their lives for the sake of our Lord Jesus Christ.
051527 We have therefore sent Judas and Silas, who themselves will tell you the same things by word of mouth.
051528 For it has seemed good to the Holy Spirit and to us to lay upon you no greater burden than these necessary things:
051529 that you abstain from what has been sacrificed to idols and from blood and from what is strangled and from unchastity. If you keep yourselves from these, you will do well. Farewell."
051530 So when they were sent off, they went down to Antioch; and having gathered the congregation together, they delivered the letter.
051531 And when they read it, they rejoiced at the exhortation.
051532 And Judas and Silas, who were themselves prophets, exhorted the brethren with many words and strengthened them.
051533 And after they had spent some time, they were sent off in peace by the brethren to those who had sent them.
051534
051535 But Paul and Barnabas remained in Antioch, teaching and preaching the word of the Lord, with many others also.
051536 And after some days Paul said to Barnabas, "Come, let us return and visit the brethren in every city where we proclaimed the word of the Lord, and see how they are."
051537 And Barnabas wanted to take with them John called Mark.
051538 But Paul thought best not to take with them one who had withdrawn from them in Pamphyl'ia, and had not gone with them to the work.
051539 And there arose a sharp contention, so that they separated from each other; Barnabas took Mark with him and sailed away to Cyprus,
051540 but Paul chose Silas and departed, being commended by the brethren to the grace of the Lord.
051541 And he went through Syria and Cili'cia, strengthening the churches.
051601 And he came also to Derbe and to Lystra. A disciple was there, named Timothy, the son of a Jewish woman who was a believer; but his father was a Greek.
051602 He was well spoken of by the brethren at Lystra and Ico'nium.
051603 Paul wanted Timothy to accompany him; and he took him and circumcised him because of the Jews that were in those places, for they all knew that his father was a Greek.
051604 As they went on their way through the cities, they delivered to them for observance the decisions which had been reached by the apostles and elders who were at Jerusalem.
051605 So the churches were strengthened in the faith, and they increased in numbers daily.
051606 And they went through the region of Phry'gia and Galatia, having been forbidden by the Holy Spirit to speak the word in Asia.
051607 And when they had come opposite My'sia, they attempted to go into Bithyn'ia, but the Spirit of Jesus did not allow them;
051608 so, passing by My'sia, they went down to Tro'as.
051609 And a vision appeared to Paul in the night: a man of Macedo'nia was standing beseeching him and saying, "Come over to Macedo'nia and help us."
051610 And when he had seen the vision, immediately we sought to go on into Macedo'nia, concluding that God had called us to preach the gospel to them.
051611 Setting sail therefore from Tro'as, we made a direct voyage to Sam'othrace, and the following day to Ne-ap'olis,
051612 and from there to Philip'pi, which is the leading city of the district of Macedo'nia, and a Roman colony. We remained in this city some days;
051613 and on the sabbath day we went outside the gate to the riverside, where we supposed there was a place of prayer; and we sat down and spoke to the women who had come together.
051614 One who heard us was a woman named Lydia, from the city of Thyati'ra, a seller of purple goods, who was a worshiper of God. The Lord opened her heart to give heed to what was said by Paul.
051615 And when she was baptized, with her household, she besought us, saying, "If you have judged me to be faithful to the Lord, come to my house and stay." And she prevailed upon us.
051616 As we were going to the place of prayer, we were met by a slave girl who had a spirit of divination and brought her owners much gain by soothsaying.
051617 She followed Paul and us, crying, "These men are servants of the Most High God, who proclaim to you the way of salvation."
051618 And this she did for many days. But Paul was annoyed, and turned and said to the spirit, "I charge you in the name of Jesus Christ to come out of her." And it came out that very hour.
051619 But when her owners saw that their hope of gain was gone, they seized Paul and Silas and dragged them into the market place before the rulers;
051620 and when they had brought them to the magistrates they said, "These men are Jews and they are disturbing our city.
051621 They advocate customs which it is not lawful for us Romans to accept or practice."
051622 The crowd joined in attacking them; and the magistrates tore the garments off them and gave orders to beat them with rods.
051623 And when they had inflicted many blows upon them, they threw them into prison, charging the jailer to keep them safely.
051624 Having received this charge, he put them into the inner prison and fastened their feet in the stocks.
051625 But about midnight Paul and Silas were praying and singing hymns to God, and the prisoners were listening to them,
051626 and suddenly there was a great earthquake, so that the foundations of the prison were shaken; and immediately all the doors were opened and every one's fetters were unfastened.
051627 When the jailer woke and saw that the prison doors were open, he drew his sword and was about to kill himself, supposing that the prisoners had escaped.
051628 But Paul cried with a loud voice, "Do not harm yourself, for we are all here."
051629 And he called for lights and rushed in, and trembling with fear he fell down before Paul and Silas,
051630 and brought them out and said, "Men, what must I do to be saved?"
051631 And they said, "Believe in the Lord Jesus, and you will be saved, you and your household."
051632 And they spoke the word of the Lord to him and to all that were in his house.
051633 And he took them the same hour of the night, and washed their wounds, and he was baptized at once, with all his family.
051634 Then he brought them up into his house, and set food before them; and he rejoiced with all his household that he had believed in God.
051635 But when it was day, the magistrates sent the police, saying, "Let those men go."
051636 And the jailer reported the words to Paul, saying, "The magistrates have sent to let you go; now therefore come out and go in peace."
051637 But Paul said to them, "They have beaten us publicly, uncondemned, men who are Roman citizens, and have thrown us into prison; and do they now cast us out secretly? No! let them come themselves and take us out."
051638 The police reported these words to the magistrates, and they were afraid when they heard that they were Roman citizens;
051639 so they came and apologized to them. And they took them out and asked them to leave the city.
051640 So they went out of the prison, and visited Lydia; and when they had seen the brethren, they exhorted them and departed.
051701 Now when they had passed through Amphip'olis and Apollo'nia, they came to Thessaloni'ca, where there was a synagogue of the Jews.
051702 And Paul went in, as was his custom, and for three weeks he argued with them from the scriptures,
051703 explaining and proving that it was necessary for the Christ to suffer and to rise from the dead, and saying, "This Jesus, whom I proclaim to you, is the Christ."
051704 And some of them were persuaded, and joined Paul and Silas; as did a great many of the devout Greeks and not a few of the leading women.
051705 But the Jews were jealous, and taking some wicked fellows of the rabble, they gathered a crowd, set the city in an uproar, and attacked the house of Jason, seeking to bring them out to the people.
051706 And when they could not find them, they dragged Jason and some of the brethren before the city authorities, crying, "These men who have turned the world upside down have come here also,
051707 and Jason has received them; and they are all acting against the decrees of Caesar, saying that there is another king, Jesus."
051708 And the people and the city authorities were disturbed when they heard this.
051709 And when they had taken security from Jason and the rest, they let them go.
051710 The brethren immediately sent Paul and Silas away by night to Beroe'a; and when they arrived they went into the Jewish synagogue.
051711 Now these Jews were more noble than those in Thessaloni'ca, for they received the word with all eagerness, examining the scriptures daily to see if these things were so.
051712 Many of them therefore believed, with not a few Greek women of high standing as well as men.
051713 But when the Jews of Thessaloni'ca learned that the word of God was proclaimed by Paul at Beroe'a also, they came there too, stirring up and inciting the crowds.
051714 Then the brethren immediately sent Paul off on his way to the sea, but Silas and Timothy remained there.
051715 Those who conducted Paul brought him as far as Athens; and receiving a command for Silas and Timothy to come to him as soon as possible, they departed.
051716 Now while Paul was waiting for them at Athens, his spirit was provoked within him as he saw that the city was full of idols.
051717 So he argued in the synagogue with the Jews and the devout persons, and in the market place every day with those who chanced to be there.
051718 Some also of the Epicurean and Stoic philosophers met him. And some said, "What would this babbler say?" Others said, "He seems to be a preacher of foreign divinities" -- because he preached Jesus and the resurrection.
051719 And they took hold of him and brought him to the Are-op'agus, saying, "May we know what this new teaching is which you present?
051720 For you bring some strange things to our ears; we wish to know therefore what these things mean."
051721 Now all the Athenians and the foreigners who lived there spent their time in nothing except telling or hearing something new.
051722 So Paul, standing in the middle of the Are-op'agus, said: "Men of Athens, I perceive that in every way you are very religious.
051723 For as I passed along, and observed the objects of your worship, I found also an altar with this inscription, 'To an unknown god.' What therefore you worship as unknown, this I proclaim to you.
051724 The God who made the world and everything in it, being Lord of heaven and earth, does not live in shrines made by man,
051725 nor is he served by human hands, as though he needed anything, since he himself gives to all men life and breath and everything.
051726 And he made from one every nation of men to live on all the face of the earth, having determined allotted periods and the boundaries of their habitation,
051727 that they should seek God, in the hope that they might feel after him and find him. Yet he is not far from each one of us,
051728 for 'In him we live and move and have our being'; as even some of your poets have said, 'For we are indeed his offspring.'
051729 Being then God's offspring, we ought not to think that the Deity is like gold, or silver, or stone, a representation by the art and imagination of man.
051730 The times of ignorance God overlooked, but now he commands all men everywhere to repent,
051731 because he has fixed a day on which he will judge the world in righteousness by a man whom he has appointed, and of this he has given assurance to all men by raising him from the dead."
051732 Now when they heard of the resurrection of the dead, some mocked; but others said, "We will hear you again about this."
051733 So Paul went out from among them.
051734 But some men joined him and believed, among them Dionys'ius the Are-op'agite and a woman named Dam'aris and others with them.
051801 After this he left Athens and went to Corinth.
051802 And he found a Jew named Aq'uila, a native of Pontus, lately come from Italy with his wife Priscilla, because Claudius had commanded all the Jews to leave Rome. And he went to see them;
051803 and because he was of the same trade he stayed with them, and they worked, for by trade they were tentmakers.
051804 And he argued in the synagogue every sabbath, and persuaded Jews and Greeks.
051805 When Silas and Timothy arrived from Macedo'nia, Paul was occupied with preaching, testifying to the Jews that the Christ was Jesus.
051806 And when they opposed and reviled him, he shook out his garments and said to them, "Your blood be upon your heads! I am innocent. From now on I will go to the Gentiles."
051807 And he left there and went to the house of a man named Titius Justus, a worshiper of God; his house was next door to the synagogue.
051808 Crispus, the ruler of the synagogue, believed in the Lord, together with all his household; and many of the Corinthians hearing Paul believed and were baptized.
051809 And the Lord said to Paul one night in a vision, "Do not be afraid, but speak and do not be silent;
051810 for I am with you, and no man shall attack you to harm you; for I have many people in this city."
051811 And he stayed a year and six months, teaching the word of God among them.
051812 But when Gallio was proconsul of Acha'ia, the Jews made a united attack upon Paul and brought him before the tribunal,
051813 saying, "This man is persuading men to worship God contrary to the law."
051814 But when Paul was about to open his mouth, Gallio said to the Jews, "If it were a matter of wrongdoing or vicious crime, I should have reason to bear with you, O Jews;
051815 but since it is a matter of questions about words and names and your own law, see to it yourselves; I refuse to be a judge of these things."
051816 And he drove them from the tribunal.
051817 And they all seized Sos'thenes, the ruler of the synagogue, and beat him in front of the tribunal. But Gallio paid no attention to this.
051818 After this Paul stayed many days longer, and then took leave of the brethren and sailed for Syria, and with him Priscilla and Aq'uila. At Cen'chre-ae he cut his hair, for he had a vow.
051819 And they came to Ephesus, and he left them there; but he himself went into the synagogue and argued with the Jews.
051820 When they asked him to stay for a longer period, he declined;
051821 but on taking leave of them he said, "I will return to you if God wills," and he set sail from Ephesus.
051822 When he had landed at Caesare'a, he went up and greeted the church, and then went down to Antioch.
051823 After spending some time there he departed and went from place to place through the region of Galatia and Phryg'ia, strengthening all the disciples.
051824 Now a Jew named Apol'los, a native of Alexandria, came to Ephesus. He was an eloquent man, well versed in the scriptures.
051825 He had been instructed in the way of the Lord; and being fervent in spirit, he spoke and taught accurately the things concerning Jesus, though he knew only the baptism of John.
051826 He began to speak boldly in the synagogue; but when Priscilla and Aq'uila heard him, they took him and expounded to him the way of God more accurately.
051827 And when he wished to cross to Acha'ia, the brethren encouraged him, and wrote to the disciples to receive him. When he arrived, he greatly helped those who through grace had believed,
051828 for he powerfully confuted the Jews in public, showing by the scriptures that the Christ was Jesus.
051901 While Apol'los was at Corinth, Paul passed through the upper country and came to Ephesus. There he found some disciples.
051902 And he said to them, "Did you receive the Holy Spirit when you believed?" And they said, "No, we have never even heard that there is a Holy Spirit."
051903 And he said, "Into what then were you baptized?" They said, "Into John's baptism."
051904 And Paul said, "John baptized with the baptism of repentance, telling the people to believe in the one who was to come after him, that is, Jesus."
051905 On hearing this, they were baptized in the name of the Lord Jesus.
051906 And when Paul had laid his hands upon them, the Holy Spirit came on them; and they spoke with tongues and prophesied.
051907 There were about twelve of them in all.
051908 And he entered the synagogue and for three months spoke boldly, arguing and pleading about the kingdom of God;
051909 but when some were stubborn and disbelieved, speaking evil of the Way before the congregation, he withdrew from them, taking the disciples with him, and argued daily in the hall of Tyran'nus.
051910 This continued for two years, so that all the residents of Asia heard the word of the Lord, both Jews and Greeks.
051911 And God did extraordinary miracles by the hands of Paul,
051912 so that handkerchiefs or aprons were carried away from his body to the sick, and diseases left them and the evil spirits came out of them.
051913 Then some of the itinerant Jewish exorcists undertook to pronounce the name of the Lord Jesus over those who had evil spirits, saying, "I adjure you by the Jesus whom Paul preaches."
051914 Seven sons of a Jewish high priest named Sceva were doing this.
051915 But the evil spirit answered them, "Jesus I know, and Paul I know; but who are you?"
051916 And the man in whom the evil spirit was leaped on them, mastered all of them, and overpowered them, so that they fled out of that house naked and wounded.
051917 And this became known to all residents of Ephesus, both Jews and Greeks; and fear fell upon them all; and the name of the Lord Jesus was extolled.
051918 Many also of those who were now believers came, confessing and divulging their practices.
051919 And a number of those who practiced magic arts brought their books together and burned them in the sight of all; and they counted the value of them and found it came to fifty thousand pieces of silver.
051920 So the word of the Lord grew and prevailed mightily.
051921 Now after these events Paul resolved in the Spirit to pass through Macedo'nia and Acha'ia and go to Jerusalem, saying, "After I have been there, I must also see Rome."
051922 And having sent into Macedo'nia two of his helpers, Timothy and Eras'tus, he himself stayed in Asia for a while.
051923 About that time there arose no little stir concerning the Way.
051924 For a man named Deme'trius, a silversmith, who made silver shrines of Ar'temis, brought no little business to the craftsmen.
051925 These he gathered together, with the workmen of like occupation, and said, "Men, you know that from this business we have our wealth.
051926 And you see and hear that not only at Ephesus but almost throughout all Asia this Paul has persuaded and turned away a considerable company of people, saying that gods made with hands are not gods.
051927 And there is danger not only that this trade of ours may come into disrepute but also that the temple of the great goddess Ar'temis may count for nothing, and that she may even be deposed from her magnificence, she whom all Asia and the world worship."
051928 When they heard this they were enraged, and cried out, "Great is Ar'temis of the Ephesians!"
051929 So the city was filled with the confusion; and they rushed together into the theater, dragging with them Ga'ius and Aristar'chus, Macedo'nians who were Paul's companions in travel.
051930 Paul wished to go in among the crowd, but the disciples would not let him;
051931 some of the A'si-archs also, who were friends of his, sent to him and begged him not to venture into the theater.
051932 Now some cried one thing, some another; for the assembly was in confusion, and most of them did not know why they had come together.
051933 Some of the crowd prompted Alexander, whom the Jews had put forward. And Alexander motioned with his hand, wishing to make a defense to the people.
051934 But when they recognized that he was a Jew, for about two hours they all with one voice cried out, "Great is Ar'temis of the Ephesians!"
051935 And when the town clerk had quieted the crowd, he said, "Men of Ephesus, what man is there who does not know that the city of the Ephesians is temple keeper of the great Ar'temis, and of the sacred stone that fell from the sky?
051936 Seeing then that these things cannot be contradicted, you ought to be quiet and do nothing rash.
051937 For you have brought these men here who are neither sacrilegious nor blasphemers of our goddess.
051938 If therefore Deme'trius and the craftsmen with him have a complaint against any one, the courts are open, and there are proconsuls; let them bring charges against one another.
051939 But if you seek anything further, it shall be settled in the regular assembly.
051940 For we are in danger of being charged with rioting today, there being no cause that we can give to justify this commotion."
051941 And when he had said this, he dismissed the assembly.
052001 After the uproar ceased, Paul sent for the disciples and having exhorted them took leave of them and departed for Macedo'nia.
052002 When he had gone through these parts and had given them much encouragement, he came to Greece.
052003 There he spent three months, and when a plot was made against him by the Jews as he was about to set sail for Syria, he determined to return through Macedo'nia.
052004 Sop'ater of Beroe'a, the son of Pyrrhus, accompanied him; and of the Thessalo'nians, Aristar'chus and Secun'dus; and Ga'ius of Derbe, and Timothy; and the Asians, Tych'icus and Troph'imus.
052005 These went on and were waiting for us at Tro'as,
052006 but we sailed away from Philip'pi after the days of Unleavened Bread, and in five days we came to them at Tro'as, where we stayed for seven days.
052007 On the first day of the week, when we were gathered together to break bread, Paul talked with them, intending to depart on the morrow; and he prolonged his speech until midnight.
052008 There were many lights in the upper chamber where we were gathered.
052009 And a young man named Eu'tychus was sitting in the window. He sank into a deep sleep as Paul talked still longer; and being overcome by sleep, he fell down from the third story and was taken up dead.
052010 But Paul went down and bent over him, and embracing him said, "Do not be alarmed, for his life is in him."
052011 And when Paul had gone up and had broken bread and eaten, he conversed with them a long while, until daybreak, and so departed.
052012 And they took the lad away alive, and were not a little comforted.
052013 But going ahead to the ship, we set sail for Assos, intending to take Paul aboard there; for so he had arranged, intending himself to go by land.
052014 And when he met us at Assos, we took him on board and came to Mityle'ne.
052015 And sailing from there we came the following day opposite Chi'os; the next day we touched at Samos; and the day after that we came to Mile'tus.
052016 For Paul had decided to sail past Ephesus, so that he might not have to spend time in Asia; for he was hastening to be at Jerusalem, if possible, on the day of Pentecost.
052017 And from Mile'tus he sent to Ephesus and called to him the elders of the church.
052018 And when they came to him, he said to them: "You yourselves know how I lived among you all the time from the first day that I set foot in Asia,
052019 serving the Lord with all humility and with tears and with trials which befell me through the plots of the Jews;
052020 how I did not shrink from declaring to you anything that was profitable, and teaching you in public and from house to house,
052021 testifying both to Jews and to Greeks of repentance to God and of faith in our Lord Jesus Christ.
052022 And now, behold, I am going to Jerusalem, bound in the Spirit, not knowing what shall befall me there;
052023 except that the Holy Spirit testifies to me in every city that imprisonment and afflictions await me.
052024 But I do not account my life of any value nor as precious to myself, if only I may accomplish my course and the ministry which I received from the Lord Jesus, to testify to the gospel of the grace of God.
052025 And now, behold, I know that all you among whom I have gone preaching the kingdom will see my face no more.
052026 Therefore I testify to you this day that I am innocent of the blood of all of you,
052027 for I did not shrink from declaring to you the whole counsel of God.
052028 Take heed to yourselves and to all the flock, in which the Holy Spirit has made you overseers, to care for the church of God which he obtained with the blood of his own Son.
052029 I know that after my departure fierce wolves will come in among you, not sparing the flock;
052030 and from among your own selves will arise men speaking perverse things, to draw away the disciples after them.
052031 Therefore be alert, remembering that for three years I did not cease night or day to admonish every one with tears.
052032 And now I commend you to God and to the word of his grace, which is able to build you up and to give you the inheritance among all those who are sanctified.
052033 I coveted no one's silver or gold or apparel.
052034 You yourselves know that these hands ministered to my necessities, and to those who were with me.
052035 In all things I have shown you that by so toiling one must help the weak, remembering the words of the Lord Jesus, how he said, 'It is more blessed to give than to receive.'"
052036 And when he had spoken thus, he knelt down and prayed with them all.
052037 And they all wept and embraced Paul and kissed him,
052038 sorrowing most of all because of the word he had spoken, that they should see his face no more. And they brought him to the ship.
052101 And when we had parted from them and set sail, we came by a straight course to Cos, and the next day to Rhodes, and from there to Pat'ara.
052102 And having found a ship crossing to Phoeni'cia, we went aboard, and set sail.
052103 When we had come in sight of Cyprus, leaving it on the left we sailed to Syria, and landed at Tyre; for there the ship was to unload its cargo.
052104 And having sought out the disciples, we stayed there for seven days. Through the Spirit they told Paul not to go on to Jerusalem.
052105 And when our days there were ended, we departed and went on our journey; and they all, with wives and children, brought us on our way till we were outside the city; and kneeling down on the beach we prayed and bade one another farewell.
052106 Then we went on board the ship, and they returned home.
052107 When we had finished the voyage from Tyre, we arrived at Ptolema'is; and we greeted the brethren and stayed with them for one day.
052108 On the morrow we departed and came to Caesare'a; and we entered the house of Philip the evangelist, who was one of the seven, and stayed with him.
052109 And he had four unmarried daughters, who prophesied.
052110 While we were staying for some days, a prophet named Ag'abus came down from Judea.
052111 And coming to us he took Paul's girdle and bound his own feet and hands, and said, "Thus says the Holy Spirit, 'So shall the Jews at Jerusalem bind the man who owns this girdle and deliver him into the hands of the Gentiles.'"
052112 When we heard this, we and the people there begged him not to go up to Jerusalem.
052113 Then Paul answered, "What are you doing, weeping and breaking my heart? For I am ready not only to be imprisoned but even to die at Jerusalem for the name of the Lord Jesus."
052114 And when he would not be persuaded, we ceased and said, "The will of the Lord be done."
052115 After these days we made ready and went up to Jerusalem.
052116 And some of the disciples from Caesare'a went with us, bringing us to the house of Mnason of Cyprus, an early disciple, with whom we should lodge.
052117 When we had come to Jerusalem, the brethren received us gladly.
052118 On the following day Paul went in with us to James; and all the elders were present.
052119 After greeting them, he related one by one the things that God had done among the Gentiles through his ministry.
052120 And when they heard it, they glorified God. And they said to him, "You see, brother, how many thousands there are among the Jews of those who have believed; they are all zealous for the law,
052121 and they have been told about you that you teach all the Jews who are among the Gentiles to forsake Moses, telling them not to circumcise their children or observe the customs.
052122 What then is to be done? They will certainly hear that you have come.
052123 Do therefore what we tell you. We have four men who are under a vow;
052124 take these men and purify yourself along with them and pay their expenses, so that they may shave their heads. Thus all will know that there is nothing in what they have been told about you but that you yourself live in observance of the law.
052125 But as for the Gentiles who have believed, we have sent a letter with our judgment that they should abstain from what has been sacrificed to idols and from blood and from what is strangled and from unchastity."
052126 Then Paul took the men, and the next day he purified himself with them and went into the temple, to give notice when the days of purification would be fulfilled and the offering presented for every one of them.
052127 When the seven days were almost completed, the Jews from Asia, who had seen him in the temple, stirred up all the crowd, and laid hands on him,
052128 crying out, "Men of Israel, help! This is the man who is teaching men everywhere against the people and the law and this place; moreover he also brought Greeks into the temple, and he has defiled this holy place."
052129 For they had previously seen Troph'imus the Ephesian with him in the city, and they supposed that Paul had brought him into the temple.
052130 Then all the city was aroused, and the people ran together; they seized Paul and dragged him out of the temple, and at once the gates were shut.
052131 And as they were trying to kill him, word came to the tribune of the cohort that all Jerusalem was in confusion.
052132 He at once took soldiers and centurions, and ran down to them; and when they saw the tribune and the soldiers, they stopped beating Paul.
052133 Then the tribune came up and arrested him, and ordered him to be bound with two chains. He inquired who he was and what he had done.
052134 Some in the crowd shouted one thing, some another; and as he could not learn the facts because of the uproar, he ordered him to be brought into the barracks.
052135 And when he came to the steps, he was actually carried by the soldiers because of the violence of the crowd;
052136 for the mob of the people followed, crying, "Away with him!"
052137 As Paul was about to be brought into the barracks, he said to the tribune, "May I say something to you?" And he said, "Do you know Greek?
052138 Are you not the Egyptian, then, who recently stirred up a revolt and led the four thousand men of the Assassins out into the wilderness?"
052139 Paul replied, "I am a Jew, from Tarsus in Cili'cia, a citizen of no mean city; I beg you, let me speak to the people."
052140 And when he had given him leave, Paul, standing on the steps, motioned with his hand to the people; and when there was a great hush, he spoke to them in the Hebrew language, saying:
052201 "Brethren and fathers, hear the defense which I now make before you."
052202 And when they heard that he addressed them in the Hebrew language, they were the more quiet. And he said:
052203 "I am a Jew, born at Tarsus in Cili'cia, but brought up in this city at the feet of Gama'li-el, educated according to the strict manner of the law of our fathers, being zealous for God as you all are this day.
052204 I persecuted this Way to the death, binding and delivering to prison both men and women,
052205 as the high priest and the whole council of elders bear me witness. From them I received letters to the brethren, and I journeyed to Damascus to take those also who were there and bring them in bonds to Jerusalem to be punished.
052206 "As I made my journey and drew near to Damascus, about noon a great light from heaven suddenly shone about me.
052207 And I fell to the ground and heard a voice saying to me, 'Saul, Saul, why do you persecute me?'
052208 And I answered, 'Who are you, Lord?' And he said to me, 'I am Jesus of Nazareth whom you are persecuting.'
052209 Now those who were with me saw the light but did not hear the voice of the one who was speaking to me.
052210 And I said, 'What shall I do, Lord?' And the Lord said to me, 'Rise, and go into Damascus, and there you will be told all that is appointed for you to do.'
052211 And when I could not see because of the brightness of that light, I was led by the hand by those who were with me, and came into Damascus.
052212 "And one Anani'as, a devout man according to the law, well spoken of by all the Jews who lived there,
052213 came to me, and standing by me said to me, 'Brother Saul, receive your sight.' And in that very hour I received my sight and saw him.
052214 And he said, 'The God of our fathers appointed you to know his will, to see the Just One and to hear a voice from his mouth;
052215 for you will be a witness for him to all men of what you have seen and heard.
052216 And now why do you wait? Rise and be baptized, and wash away your sins, calling on his name.'
052217 "When I had returned to Jerusalem and was praying in the temple, I fell into a trance
052218 and saw him saying to me, 'Make haste and get quickly out of Jerusalem, because they will not accept your testimony about me.'
052219 And I said, 'Lord, they themselves know that in every synagogue I imprisoned and beat those who believed in thee.
052220 And when the blood of Stephen thy witness was shed, I also was standing by and approving, and keeping the garments of those who killed him.'
052221 And he said to me, 'Depart; for I will send you far away to the Gentiles.'"
052222 Up to this word they listened to him; then they lifted up their voices and said, "Away with such a fellow from the earth! For he ought not to live."
052223 And as they cried out and waved their garments and threw dust into the air,
052224 the tribune commanded him to be brought into the barracks, and ordered him to be examined by scourging, to find out why they shouted thus against him.
052225 But when they had tied him up with the thongs, Paul said to the centurion who was standing by, "Is it lawful for you to scourge a man who is a Roman citizen, and uncondemned?"
052226 When the centurion heard that, he went to the tribune and said to him, "What are you about to do? For this man is a Roman citizen."
052227 So the tribune came and said to him, "Tell me, are you a Roman citizen?" And he said, "Yes."
052228 The tribune answered, "I bought this citizenship for a large sum." Paul said, "But I was born a citizen."
052229 So those who were about to examine him withdrew from him instantly; and the tribune also was afraid, for he realized that Paul was a Roman citizen and that he had bound him.
052230 But on the morrow, desiring to know the real reason why the Jews accused him, he unbound him, and commanded the chief priests and all the council to meet, and he brought Paul down and set him before them.
052301 And Paul, looking intently at the council, said, "Brethren, I have lived before God in all good conscience up to this day."
052302 And the high priest Anani'as commanded those who stood by him to strike him on the mouth.
052303 Then Paul said to him, "God shall strike you, you whitewashed wall! Are you sitting to judge me according to the law, and yet contrary to the law you order me to be struck?"
052304 Those who stood by said, "Would you revile God's high priest?"
052305 And Paul said, "I did not know, brethren, that he was the high priest; for it is written, 'You shall not speak evil of a ruler of your people.'"
052306 But when Paul perceived that one part were Sad'ducees and the other Pharisees, he cried out in the council, "Brethren, I am a Pharisee, a son of Pharisees; with respect to the hope and the resurrection of the dead I am on trial."
052307 And when he had said this, a dissension arose between the Pharisees and the Sad'ducees; and the assembly was divided.
052308 For the Sad'ducees say that there is no resurrection, nor angel, nor spirit; but the Pharisees acknowledge them all.
052309 Then a great clamor arose; and some of the scribes of the Pharisees' party stood up and contended, "We find nothing wrong in this man. What if a spirit or an angel spoke to him?"
052310 And when the dissension became violent, the tribune, afraid that Paul would be torn in pieces by them, commanded the soldiers to go down and take him by force from among them and bring him into the barracks.
052311 The following night the Lord stood by him and said, "Take courage, for as you have testified about me at Jerusalem, so you must bear witness also at Rome."
052312 When it was day, the Jews made a plot and bound themselves by an oath neither to eat nor drink till they had killed Paul.
052313 There were more than forty who made this conspiracy.
052314 And they went to the chief priests and elders, and said, "We have strictly bound ourselves by an oath to taste no food till we have killed Paul.
052315 You therefore, along with the council, give notice now to the tribune to bring him down to you, as though you were going to determine his case more exactly. And we are ready to kill him before he comes near."
052316 Now the son of Paul's sister heard of their ambush; so he went and entered the barracks and told Paul.
052317 And Paul called one of the centurions and said, "Take this young man to the tribune; for he has something to tell him."
052318 So he took him and brought him to the tribune and said, "Paul the prisoner called me and asked me to bring this young man to you, as he has something to say to you."
052319 The tribune took him by the hand, and going aside asked him privately, "What is it that you have to tell me?"
052320 And he said, "The Jews have agreed to ask you to bring Paul down to the council tomorrow, as though they were going to inquire somewhat more closely about him.
052321 But do not yield to them; for more than forty of their men lie in ambush for him, having bound themselves by an oath neither to eat nor drink till they have killed him; and now they are ready, waiting for the promise from you."
052322 So the tribune dismissed the young man, charging him, "Tell no one that you have informed me of this."
052323 Then he called two of the centurions and said, "At the third hour of the night get ready two hundred soldiers with seventy horsemen and two hundred spearmen to go as far as Caesare'a.
052324 Also provide mounts for Paul to ride, and bring him safely to Felix the governor."
052325 And he wrote a letter to this effect:
052326 "Claudius Lys'ias to his Excellency the governor Felix, greeting.
052327 This man was seized by the Jews, and was about to be killed by them, when I came upon them with the soldiers and rescued him, having learned that he was a Roman citizen.
052328 And desiring to know the charge on which they accused him, I brought him down to their council.
052329 I found that he was accused about questions of their law, but charged with nothing deserving death or imprisonment.
052330 And when it was disclosed to me that there would be a plot against the man, I sent him to you at once, ordering his accusers also to state before you what they have against him."
052331 So the soldiers, according to their instructions, took Paul and brought him by night to Antip'atris.
052332 And on the morrow they returned to the barracks, leaving the horsemen to go on with him.
052333 When they came to Caesare'a and delivered the letter to the governor, they presented Paul also before him.
052334 On reading the letter, he asked to what province he belonged. When he learned that he was from Cili'cia
052335 he said, "I will hear you when your accusers arrive." And he commanded him to be guarded in Herod's praetorium.
052401 And after five days the high priest Anani'as came down with some elders and a spokesman, one Tertul'lus. They laid before the governor their case against Paul;
052402 and when he was called, Tertul'lus began to accuse him, saying: "Since through you we enjoy much peace, and since by your provision, most excellent Felix, reforms are introduced on behalf of this nation,
052403 in every way and everywhere we accept this with all gratitude.
052404 But, to detain you no further, I beg you in your kindness to hear us briefly.
052405 For we have found this man a pestilent fellow, an agitator among all the Jews throughout the world, and a ringleader of the sect of the Nazarenes.
052406 He even tried to profane the temple, but we seized him.
052407
052408 By examining him yourself you will be able to learn from him about everything of which we accuse him."
052409 The Jews also joined in the charge, affirming that all this was so.
052410 And when the governor had motioned to him to speak, Paul replied: "Realizing that for many years you have been judge over this nation, I cheerfully make my defense.
052411 As you may ascertain, it is not more than twelve days since I went up to worship at Jerusalem;
052412 and they did not find me disputing with any one or stirring up a crowd, either in the temple or in the synagogues, or in the city.
052413 Neither can they prove to you what they now bring up against me.
052414 But this I admit to you, that according to the Way, which they call a sect, I worship the God of our fathers, believing everything laid down by the law or written in the prophets,
052415 having a hope in God which these themselves accept, that there will be a resurrection of both the just and the unjust.
052416 So I always take pains to have a clear conscience toward God and toward men.
052417 Now after some years I came to bring to my nation alms and offerings.
052418 As I was doing this, they found me purified in the temple, without any crowd or tumult. But some Jews from Asia --
052419 they ought to be here before you and to make an accusation, if they have anything against me.
052420 Or else let these men themselves say what wrongdoing they found when I stood before the council,
052421 except this one thing which I cried out while standing among them, 'With respect to the resurrection of the dead I am on trial before you this day.'"
052422 But Felix, having a rather accurate knowledge of the Way, put them off, saying, "When Lys'ias the tribune comes down, I will decide your case."
052423 Then he gave orders to the centurion that he should be kept in custody but should have some liberty, and that none of his friends should be prevented from attending to his needs.
052424 After some days Felix came with his wife Drusil'la, who was a Jewess; and he sent for Paul and heard him speak upon faith in Christ Jesus.
052425 And as he argued about justice and self-control and future judgment, Felix was alarmed and said, "Go away for the present; when I have an opportunity I will summon you."
052426 At the same time he hoped that money would be given him by Paul. So he sent for him often and conversed with him.
052427 But when two years had elapsed, Felix was succeeded by Porcius Festus; and desiring to do the Jews a favor, Felix left Paul in prison.
052501 Now when Festus had come into his province, after three days he went up to Jerusalem from Caesare'a.
052502 And the chief priests and the principal men of the Jews informed him against Paul; and they urged him,
052503 asking as a favor to have the man sent to Jerusalem, planning an ambush to kill him on the way.
052504 Festus replied that Paul was being kept at Caesare'a, and that he himself intended to go there shortly.
052505 "So," said he, "let the men of authority among you go down with me, and if there is anything wrong about the man, let them accuse him."
052506 When he had stayed among them not more than eight or ten days, he went down to Caesare'a; and the next day he took his seat on the tribunal and ordered Paul to be brought.
052507 And when he had come, the Jews who had gone down from Jerusalem stood about him, bringing against him many serious charges which they could not prove.
052508 Paul said in his defense, "Neither against the law of the Jews, nor against the temple, nor against Caesar have I offended at all."
052509 But Festus, wishing to do the Jews a favor, said to Paul, "Do you wish to go up to Jerusalem, and there be tried on these charges before me?"
052510 But Paul said, "I am standing before Caesar's tribunal, where I ought to be tried; to the Jews I have done no wrong, as you know very well.
052511 If then I am a wrongdoer, and have committed anything for which I deserve to die, I do not seek to escape death; but if there is nothing in their charges against me, no one can give me up to them. I appeal to Caesar."
052512 Then Festus, when he had conferred with his council, answered, "You have appealed to Caesar; to Caesar you shall go."
052513 Now when some days had passed, Agrippa the king and Berni'ce arrived at Caesare'a to welcome Festus.
052514 And as they stayed there many days, Festus laid Paul's case before the king, saying, "There is a man left prisoner by Felix;
052515 and when I was at Jerusalem, the chief priests and the elders of the Jews gave information about him, asking for sentence against him.
052516 I answered them that it was not the custom of the Romans to give up any one before the accused met the accusers face to face, and had opportunity to make his defense concerning the charge laid against him.
052517 When therefore they came together here, I made no delay, but on the next day took my seat on the tribunal and ordered the man to be brought in.
052518 When the accusers stood up, they brought no charge in his case of such evils as I supposed;
052519 but they had certain points of dispute with him about their own superstition and about one Jesus, who was dead, but whom Paul asserted to be alive.
052520 Being at a loss how to investigate these questions, I asked whether he wished to go to Jerusalem and be tried there regarding them.
052521 But when Paul had appealed to be kept in custody for the decision of the emperor, I commanded him to be held until I could send him to Caesar."
052522 And Agrippa said to Festus, "I should like to hear the man myself." "Tomorrow," said he, "you shall hear him."
052523 So on the morrow Agrippa and Berni'ce came with great pomp, and they entered the audience hall with the military tribunes and the prominent men of the city. Then by command of Festus Paul was brought in.
052524 And Festus said, "King Agrippa and all who are present with us, you see this man about whom the whole Jewish people petitioned me, both at Jerusalem and here, shouting that he ought not to live any longer.
052525 But I found that he had done nothing deserving death; and as he himself appealed to the emperor, I decided to send him.
052526 But I have nothing definite to write to my lord about him. Therefore I have brought him before you, and, especially before you, King Agrippa, that, after we have examined him, I may have something to write.
052527 For it seems to me unreasonable, in sending a prisoner, not to indicate the charges against him."
052601 Agrippa said to Paul, "You have permission to speak for yourself." Then Paul stretched out his hand and made his defense:
052602 "I think myself fortunate that it is before you, King Agrippa, I am to make my defense today against all the accusations of the Jews,
052603 because you are especially familiar with all customs and controversies of the Jews; therefore I beg you to listen to me patiently.
052604 "My manner of life from my youth, spent from the beginning among my own nation and at Jerusalem, is known by all the Jews.
052605 They have known for a long time, if they are willing to testify, that according to the strictest party of our religion I have lived as a Pharisee.
052606 And now I stand here on trial for hope in the promise made by God to our fathers,
052607 to which our twelve tribes hope to attain, as they earnestly worship night and day. And for this hope I am accused by Jews, O king!
052608 Why is it thought incredible by any of you that God raises the dead?
052609 "I myself was convinced that I ought to do many things in opposing the name of Jesus of Nazareth.
052610 And I did so in Jerusalem; I not only shut up many of the saints in prison, by authority from the chief priests, but when they were put to death I cast my vote against them.
052611 And I punished them often in all the synagogues and tried to make them blaspheme; and in raging fury against them, I persecuted them even to foreign cities.
052612 "Thus I journeyed to Damascus with the authority and commission of the chief priests.
052613 At midday, O king, I saw on the way a light from heaven, brighter than the sun, shining round me and those who journeyed with me.
052614 And when we had all fallen to the ground, I heard a voice saying to me in the Hebrew language, 'Saul, Saul, why do you persecute me? It hurts you to kick against the goads.'
052615 And I said, 'Who are you, Lord?' And the Lord said, 'I am Jesus whom you are persecuting.
052616 But rise and stand upon your feet; for I have appeared to you for this purpose, to appoint you to serve and bear witness to the things in which you have seen me and to those in which I will appear to you,
052617 delivering you from the people and from the Gentiles -- to whom I send you
052618 to open their eyes, that they may turn from darkness to light and from the power of Satan to God, that they may receive forgiveness of sins and a place among those who are sanctified by faith in me.'
052619 "Wherefore, O King Agrippa, I was not disobedient to the heavenly vision,
052620 but declared first to those at Damascus, then at Jerusalem and throughout all the country of Judea, and also to the Gentiles, that they should repent and turn to God and perform deeds worthy of their repentance.
052621 For this reason the Jews seized me in the temple and tried to kill me.
052622 To this day I have had the help that comes from God, and so I stand here testifying both to small and great, saying nothing but what the prophets and Moses said would come to pass:
052623 that the Christ must suffer, and that, by being the first to rise from the dead, he would proclaim light both to the people and to the Gentiles."
052624 And as he thus made his defense, Festus said with a loud voice, "Paul, you are mad; your great learning is turning you mad."
052625 But Paul said, "I am not mad, most excellent Festus, but I am speaking the sober truth.
052626 For the king knows about these things, and to him I speak freely; for I am persuaded that none of these things has escaped his notice, for this was not done in a corner.
052627 King Agrippa, do you believe the prophets? I know that you believe."
052628 And Agrippa said to Paul, "In a short time you think to make me a Christian!"
052629 And Paul said, "Whether short or long, I would to God that not only you but also all who hear me this day might become such as I am -- except for these chains."
052630 Then the king rose, and the governor and Berni'ce and those who were sitting with them;
052631 and when they had withdrawn, they said to one another, "This man is doing nothing to deserve death or imprisonment."
052632 And Agrippa said to Festus, "This man could have been set free if he had not appealed to Caesar."
052701 And when it was decided that we should sail for Italy, they delivered Paul and some other prisoners to a centurion of the Augustan Cohort, named Julius.
052702 And embarking in a ship of Adramyt'tium, which was about to sail to the ports along the coast of Asia, we put to sea, accompanied by Aristar'chus, a Macedo'nian from Thessaloni'ca.
052703 The next day we put in at Sidon; and Julius treated Paul kindly, and gave him leave to go to his friends and be cared for.
052704 And putting to sea from there we sailed under the lee of Cyprus, because the winds were against us.
052705 And when we had sailed across the sea which is off Cili'cia and Pamphyl'ia, we came to Myra in Ly'cia.
052706 There the centurion found a ship of Alexandria sailing for Italy, and put us on board.
052707 We sailed slowly for a number of days, and arrived with difficulty off Cni'dus, and as the wind did not allow us to go on, we sailed under the lee of Crete off Salmo'ne.
052708 Coasting along it with difficulty, we came to a place called Fair Havens, near which was the city of Lase'a.
052709 As much time had been lost, and the voyage was already dangerous because the fast had already gone by, Paul advised them,
052710 saying, "Sirs, I perceive that the voyage will be with injury and much loss, not only of the cargo and the ship, but also of our lives."
052711 But the centurion paid more attention to the captain and to the owner of the ship than to what Paul said.
052712 And because the harbor was not suitable to winter in, the majority advised to put to sea from there, on the chance that somehow they could reach Phoenix, a harbor of Crete, looking northeast and southeast, and winter there.
052713 And when the south wind blew gently, supposing that they had obtained their purpose, they weighed anchor and sailed along Crete, close inshore.
052714 But soon a tempestuous wind, called the northeaster, struck down from the land;
052715 and when the ship was caught and could not face the wind, we gave way to it and were driven.
052716 And running under the lee of a small island called Cauda, we managed with difficulty to secure the boat;
052717 after hoisting it up, they took measures to undergird the ship; then, fearing that they should run on the Syr'tis, they lowered the gear, and so were driven.
052718 As we were violently storm-tossed, they began next day to throw the cargo overboard;
052719 and the third day they cast out with their own hands the tackle of the ship.
052720 And when neither sun nor stars appeared for many a day, and no small tempest lay on us, all hope of our being saved was at last abandoned.
052721 As they had been long without food, Paul then came forward among them and said, "Men, you should have listened to me, and should not have set sail from Crete and incurred this injury and loss.
052722 I now bid you take heart; for there will be no loss of life among you, but only of the ship.
052723 For this very night there stood by me an angel of the God to whom I belong and whom I worship,
052724 and he said, 'Do not be afraid, Paul; you must stand before Caesar; and lo, God has granted you all those who sail with you.'
052725 So take heart, men, for I have faith in God that it will be exactly as I have been told.
052726 But we shall have to run on some island."
052727 When the fourteenth night had come, as we were drifting across the sea of A'dria, about midnight the sailors suspected that they were nearing land.
052728 So they sounded and found twenty fathoms; a little farther on they sounded again and found fifteen fathoms.
052729 And fearing that we might run on the rocks, they let out four anchors from the stern, and prayed for day to come.
052730 And as the sailors were seeking to escape from the ship, and had lowered the boat into the sea, under pretense of laying out anchors from the bow,
052731 Paul said to the centurion and the soldiers, "Unless these men stay in the ship, you cannot be saved."
052732 Then the soldiers cut away the ropes of the boat, and let it go.
052733 As day was about to dawn, Paul urged them all to take some food, saying, "Today is the fourteenth day that you have continued in suspense and without food, having taken nothing.
052734 Therefore I urge you to take some food; it will give you strength, since not a hair is to perish from the head of any of you."
052735 And when he had said this, he took bread, and giving thanks to God in the presence of all he broke it and began to eat.
052736 Then they all were encouraged and ate some food themselves.
052737 (We were in all two hundred and seventy-six persons in the ship.)
052738 And when they had eaten enough, they lightened the ship, throwing out the wheat into the sea.
052739 Now when it was day, they did not recognize the land, but they noticed a bay with a beach, on which they planned if possible to bring the ship ashore.
052740 So they cast off the anchors and left them in the sea, at the same time loosening the ropes that tied the rudders; then hoisting the foresail to the wind they made for the beach.
052741 But striking a shoal they ran the vessel aground; the bow stuck and remained immovable, and the stern was broken up by the surf.
052742 The soldiers' plan was to kill the prisoners, lest any should swim away and escape;
052743 but the centurion, wishing to save Paul, kept them from carrying out their purpose. He ordered those who could swim to throw themselves overboard first and make for the land,
052744 and the rest on planks or on pieces of the ship. And so it was that all escaped to land.
052801 After we had escaped, we then learned that the island was called Malta.
052802 And the natives showed us unusual kindness, for they kindled a fire and welcomed us all, because it had begun to rain and was cold.
052803 Paul had gathered a bundle of sticks and put them on the fire, when a viper came out because of the heat and fastened on his hand.
